  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3e223191-ccd3-4e2f-923b-9aa2087103ef'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1257459-should-you-read-the-first-book-before-you">Should you read the first book before you read the others in the series, or does it not matter?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1257459'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F5972040-beyond-the-grave">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1257459-should-you-read-the-first-book-before-you">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1257459-should-you-read-the-first-book-before-you">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37079158-rebecca"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1467659034i/37079158._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37079158-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">you should read them in order as the story progresses. Often they mention things that happened in previous books and it also helps understand the rela<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">you should read them in order as the story progresses. Often they mention things that happened in previous books and it also helps understand the relationships between the people. Also, the first book explains the whole premise of the storyline and how the hunt began.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1390558200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16033290987157155111">Beyond the Grave (The 39 Clues #4), Jude Watson<br/>Beyond the Grave is the fourth book in The 39 Clues series first published in June 2, 2009 and written by Jude Watson. Thematically the novel uses Biblical knowledge, prophecy, and spiritual topics to explore the afterlife. Amy and Dan head for Cairo, Egypt, with their au pair Nellie Gomez, to find a clue, hidden by Ekaterina founder, Katherine Cahill. They were tailed by Irina Spasky, but escape to a store with an Egyptian goddess statue, the Sakhe</span>
  <span id="freeText16033290987157155111" style="display:none">Beyond the Grave (The 39 Clues #4), Jude Watson<br />Beyond the Grave is the fourth book in The 39 Clues series first published in June 2, 2009 and written by Jude Watson. Thematically the novel uses Biblical knowledge, prophecy, and spiritual topics to explore the afterlife. Amy and Dan head for Cairo, Egypt, with their au pair Nellie Gomez, to find a clue, hidden by Ekaterina founder, Katherine Cahill. They were tailed by Irina Spasky, but escape to a store with an Egyptian goddess statue, the Sakhet. There, a man, Theo Cotter, shows up and convinces them it's a fake. Discouraged, they go back to Nellie. ...<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفتم ماه می سال 2014 میلادی؛ <br />عنوان: آن سوی گور (فراتر از گور) - کتاب چهارم از 39 سرنخ؛ نویسنده: جودی واتسن (واتسون)؛ مترجم: دلارام کارخیران؛ تهران، ویدا، چاپ دوم 1392؛ در 183 ص، شابک: 9786002910486؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان - سده 21 م<br />فراتر از گور (آنسوی گور)؛ جلد چهارم از مجموعه 39 سرنخ، اثر «جود واتسون» است. بر اساس شایعه ای «کاترینا کاهیل»، سرنخ بعدی را در مصر مخفی کرده است. بنابرهمین شایعه، «دن» و «امی»، باید برای یافتن سرنخ بعدی، به مصر بروند. آنجا باید در آثار باستانی، به گشت و گذار بپردازند. اکنون علاوه بر افراد خاندان، باید از خطرهای باستانی نیز دوری کنند...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="16033290987157155111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText540006876579158073" style="display:none">Jude Watson did a fine job of letting us in on a few more Cahill secrets, but some additional mysteries remain. Amy and Dan have found the next clue and have had a near-run-in with the dreaded Madrigals, who have smashed up the Ekat stronghold in Cairo. Allastair Oh has returned from the dead (once again), the Kabras have been led astray to Lake Tash, and Jonah Wizard and his dad are on the way to Morocco after following a false lead. Hot on their trail is bad girl ex-KGB spy Irina, and we have no idea where the Holts are. We gain a little insight into her life, too. <br /><br />SPOILER ALERT: The mystery code that begins on page 39 says: Alistair was there on the night they died. I believe this statement is referring to Amy and Dan's parents who perished in a fire. This implies that either: a) Allastair is responsible for that fire, or b) Alistair knows who killed Amy and Dan's parents.</span>

  <span id="freeText10542173600279857223" style="display:none">My favorite in the entire 39 Clues series so far. I love the educational adventure that these books bring for kids. I'm quite fascinated with Egypt's history, and since Amy and Dan Cahill find themselves in Egypt for this volume, I was happy to be reading this book. Although it doesn't come from from a Christian perspective exactly, this particular book infused something Christian-related into the plot---VERY, very good, Jude Watson! <br /><br />Now, there may have been a comment or two that I didn't quite enjoy in the story, but it all must be taken in stride. It will be a while before I read another 39 Clues book that excites me as much as this one!</span>

<div id="review_91388037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91388037" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1735763-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442495481p2/1735763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91388037?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1735763-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91388037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18239941207945567701">The chase continues as 14 year-old Amy Cahill and her 11 year-old brother Dan rush off to Cairo, Egypt in search of the next clue. You can feel the heat and smell the exotic spices as we catch up with the duo at the Khan market. Two new characters are introduced in this book, Theo, an Indiana Jones-type Egyptologist and Hilary, who is the childhood best friend of Grace, Amy and Dan’s dead grandmother. Instantly likable, they play an important part in the story.<br/><br/>Amy and Dan learn a little about Gr</span>
  <span id="freeText18239941207945567701" style="display:none">The chase continues as 14 year-old Amy Cahill and her 11 year-old brother Dan rush off to Cairo, Egypt in search of the next clue. You can feel the heat and smell the exotic spices as we catch up with the duo at the Khan market. Two new characters are introduced in this book, Theo, an Indiana Jones-type Egyptologist and Hilary, who is the childhood best friend of Grace, Amy and Dan’s dead grandmother. Instantly likable, they play an important part in the story.<br /><br />Amy and Dan learn a little about Grace’s past through Hilary who gives them a card with a message from their grandmother. But the message seems so detached they begin to question why their grandmother (whom they miss terribly) would send them on such a dangerous hunt. This doubting causes pain and friction between the brother and sister, adding internal conflict as the team escape a scary crocodile encounter, a submarine disaster, being buried alive in an Egyptian tomb, and the clutches of the Ekaterina branch members. Alistair Oh makes a brief appearance, but it is Irina Spasky who is close on their tail this time.<br /><br />In addition, it is Irina’s vulnerable side that is revealed in this book. She has a painful history attached to that of Grace, making the reader wonder what exactly happened. I’m getting really curious about Nellie Gomez, too, the children’s au pair who has the uncanny ability to get them out of scraps time and time again. She has very convenient talents. I am certain this isn’t coincidence, and I look forward to seeing how it all plays out in the next books. Finally, I was somewhat disappointed with the way things ended up with Hilary. I would have liked for this relationship to end differently.<br /><br />I must add that the titles of the books have double significance. For example, Beyond the Grave is a good indication the next clue is somewhere in a grave, but also hints at Grace’s message coming from “beyond the grave” since she is already dead when they receive it. It's a cool play on words, which, by the way, is how the clues are discovered in all the books.<br /><br />This book was another exciting adventure that has me waiting to read the next book in this fun series suitable for all ages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18239941207945567701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2898220227933699190" style="display:none">English review at bottom!<br><br><br><i>"What makes us extraordinary can sometimes makes us dangerous"</i><br><br>Los hermanitos Cahill lo han hecho de nuevo.<br>Han enfrentado los peligros y han encontrado su pista. Junto con revelaciones sobre su abuela y todo lo demás.<br>Honestamente, <i>Beyond the Grave</i> debería llamarse: <i>Slumdog Millionaire in the Kane Chronicles</i>.<br>Algunas cosas que me han gustado de este tomo:<br>- <b>Dan</b>. Nunca imaginé que vería a Dan molesto. Con su consabido sentido del humor, siempre está haciendo chistes y quejándose del calor y de que tiene hambre y que odia los museos y las bibliotecas; pero debo admitir que aquí se pasó. Se pasó por completo. Hay partes donde se pelea con Amy y es una persona completamente diferente. Me gustó muchísimo eso.<br>- <b>Irina</b>. ¿Desde cuándo la rusa tiene corazón? ¿Y marido? ¿¿¿E hijos???<br>- <b>Theo</b>. Theo es bello, lo admito. Me recuerda a Milo Thatch:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489467990i/22216962._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Me encanta como coquetea con Nellie, otp<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484786142ra/21753393.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Amó esa mezcla de Indiana Jones y Milo Thatch que tiene. Lo amé instantáneamente...<br><br>Ahora, cosas que no me gustaron:<br>- <b>Alistair</b>- Te hubieras quedado muerto, papi, please. No. Me cae mal. De paso, resucitó y los carajitos no le preguntaron "hey, papi, qué pasó? pana te perdei feo". No, nada. Absolutamente nada. Ni un "Hola, cómo te fue en el más allá? El verdadero <i>Más allá de la tumba</i> es el mardito chino ese.<br>- <b>The Madrigals</b>. ¿Qué se creen? ¿Son como una especie de súper mutantes. No si, Apocalipsis los llaman a ellos.<br>- <b>The Kabras</b>. El hecho de que los Kabra no salen aquí... ¡ESO ME TIENE MAL! De vaina y los nombran. También me caen mal por tener tantos cobres.<br><br>De resto, todo bien. Como siempre.<br>Esa diosa egipcia está loca, btw.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496026941i/22875341.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"What makes us extraordinary can sometimes makes us dangerous"</i><br><br>The Cahill siblings have done it again.<br>They have faced the dangers and have found their clue. Along with revelations about their grandmother and stuff.<br>Honestly, <i>Beyond the Grave</i> should be called: <i>Slumdog Millionaire in the Kane Chronicles</i>.<br>Some things I liked about this tome:<br>- <b>Dan</b>. I never imagined that I would see Dan upset. With his usual sense of humor, he is always making jokes and complaining about the heat and that he is hungry and that he hates museums and libraries; But I must admit that it happened here. It happened completely. There are parts where she quarrels with Amy and is a completely different person. I really liked that.<br>- <b>Irina</b>. Since when the Russian has a heart? And husband? And sons???<br>- <b>Theo</b>. Theo is beautiful, I admit. It reminds me of Milo Thatch:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489467990i/22216962._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I love when he flirts with Nellie, otp.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484786142ra/21753393.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I loved that mix of Indiana Jones and Milo Thatch that he has. I loved it instantly.<br><br>Now, things I did not like:<br>- <b>Alistair</b>. You shoud have stayed dead, honey, really. No. I do not like him. By the way, he was resurrected and the kids didn't asked him: "hey, where have you been? you died, you get lost pften, dude". No, nothing. Absolutely nothing. Not a "Hi, how was the afterlife? The real <i>Beyond the grave</i> is this fucking chinese guy.<br>- <b>The Madrigals</b>. Who they think they are? Are they kind of like super mutants. Oh, right, now thay call 'em Apocalypse.<br>- <b>The Kabra</b>. The fact that the Kabra don't come out here... ¡UPSETS ME! <br><br>Otherwise, all good. As usual.<br>That Egyptian goddess is crazy, btw.</span>

<div id="review_3118047867" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3118047867" />
    <a title="Madison H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104124564-madison-h"><img alt="Madison H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571261715p2/104124564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3118047867?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madison H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madison H." href="/user/show/104124564-madison-h">Madison H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3118047867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6603179478614737678">After reading the first three books in the series, naturally, I decided to read the fourth. This book was not necessarily better than the others, but it was not disappointing. It was a good read and added on to the adventure with Amy and Dan. The book does in fact give insight into some characters that gives them more depth and personality that allows the reader to form opinions and connections, especially with Grace. Her grandchildren, while going through this hunt, really think more and more a</span>
  <span id="freeText6603179478614737678" style="display:none">After reading the first three books in the series, naturally, I decided to read the fourth. This book was not necessarily better than the others, but it was not disappointing. It was a good read and added on to the adventure with Amy and Dan. The book does in fact give insight into some characters that gives them more depth and personality that allows the reader to form opinions and connections, especially with Grace. Her grandchildren, while going through this hunt, really think more and more about their relationship they had with her that causes them to reveal some internalized feelings both Dan and Amy had. This, I do quite enjoy because I am just curious on what she was like when she was alive as she is in fact the one that pushed all these characters into this search that really started this whole series. My only issue with it is the way it is written; it feels like a cheesy sitcom episode where they mention something that someone else does all the time when they do not and then they proceed to do so. For example, a character might say that their best friend falls all of the time then they immediately do so for the first time while walking through the door, except it is just Dan and Amy trying to make connections between their time with their grandma and a hint she might have given them during their time together. Due to this I would say that the book is more for younger children that are around ten that would not notice such a detail but still be able to comprehend and understand what is going on throughout the plot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6603179478614737678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5026613887046702253" style="display:none">The chase continues for the 39 clues. Amy and Dan are two very interesting characters. Although the book is adventurous it seems that they are handed the clues and don’t really have to look for them. Alaster Oh comes back from the dead once again and is still trying to team up with Amy and Dan. Why? This is a very nail-biting story, but it still does have some slow moving chapters. Although the book gives lots of background on the twins, it lacks background on the “madrigals”. They still get betrayed by people who they “thought” they could trust. This book is still a very good book with or without the confusing parts.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alix" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alix" href="/user/show/23691352-alix">Alix</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer873656939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer612719575369461219"><br/><br/>I like the book 39 clues”Beyond the Grave” by Jude Watson, because there are a lot of intense situation that happen throughout the book. This is number four in the series.The last book leaves Dan and Amy trapped in a cave. This book continues from there. This book shows you how kids can figure things out by using what they have for resources. It also deals with American history.<br/><br/> Dan and Amy are still in the lead to win the race to be the most powerful family in the world. Someone is always fight</span>
  <span id="freeText612719575369461219" style="display:none"><br /><br />I like the book 39 clues”Beyond the Grave” by Jude Watson, because there are a lot of intense situation that happen throughout the book. This is number four in the series.The last book leaves Dan and Amy trapped in a cave. This book continues from there. This book shows you how kids can figure things out by using what they have for resources. It also deals with American history.<br /><br /> Dan and Amy are still in the lead to win the race to be the most powerful family in the world. Someone is always fighting to stay afloat in this competition. Dan and Amy next clue lead them to a museum in Egypt . When they get to the museum they find their next clue behind a brick in the museum wall. Dan pulls out a brick and the security guard sees him do it . Dan threw the brick at the security guard so they could escape. The clue was a map and a key. The key they found opened the door to one of the rooms in their hotel. Behind the door there were plans for a doomsday device. This is when it gets very exciting.<br /> <br /><br />39 Clues “Beyond the Grave” takes place in modern day Cairo, Egypt.The book 39 clues “Beyond the grave”shows how you have to figure out some of the clues. It makes your mind think as you read how you would try and figure out some of the clues. <br />	<br />Trusting no one is more dangerous than just trusting one person. Dan and Amy though they could trust their cousin Natalie, but she ran off with the clue they team up to find. <br />	<br />I would recommend this book for any body that likes adventure books. If you like series there are more book that continue from this book. In the 39 clues beyond the grave there are lot of serious situations this book would be great for eighth grade and up.<br />I think some adults would enjoy the 39 Clues series also. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1212796-heather?shelf=school-books-kid-books">school-books-kid-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445052528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9404385592957113817">I'm going to give a generic review of the series. Basically because I'm lazy and don't want to write 39 reviews. Okay, 11.<br/><br/>We finally read Book 1. And then because we liked it so well, the entire series. One son (age 12) has read them all, the second son (also age 12) is on Book 2. And son #3 (age 8) will be starting as soon as he finishes his current book.<br/><br/>I thought the premise of this book very interesting. I loved how they integrated history and geography along with problem-solving skills and c</span>
  <span id="freeText9404385592957113817" style="display:none">I'm going to give a generic review of the series. Basically because I'm lazy and don't want to write 39 reviews. Okay, 11.<br /><br />We finally read Book 1. And then because we liked it so well, the entire series. One son (age 12) has read them all, the second son (also age 12) is on Book 2. And son #3 (age 8) will be starting as soon as he finishes his current book.<br /><br />I thought the premise of this book very interesting. I loved how they integrated history and geography along with problem-solving skills and code cracking. Add in the action, humor and intrigue and kids (and some adults) can't put them down. All three of us that have read 39 Clues thought Book 2 the weakest of the series. But as one son said, after finishing the series, "Gordon Korman seems to be getting better. I think he's a decent author now." <br /><br />Some of the books are better at teaching the history part, others just barely skim the surface and you don't really learn about the person they're 'highlighting'. I appreciate that they're clean books - no curse words or you-know-what going on. There is some violence (very little, if any, blood) and several murder attempts, but they never work.<br /><br />The series would most likely be called twaddle by my Charlotte Mason friends. I do, however, think it has more redeeming qualities than most kids literature and I'm happy to see my boys devouring a book every day or so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9404385592957113817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_315504808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315504808" />
    <a title="Beaulah Pragg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5738996-beaulah-pragg"><img alt="Beaulah Pragg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518244257p2/5738996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315504808?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beaulah Pragg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beaulah Pragg" href="/user/show/5738996-beaulah-pragg">Beaulah Pragg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315504808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12015539840384823541">Another excellent book in this ever developing series. I love that reading this book as a young adult, I still get a lot of value and enjoyment out of it. The cover even looks sophisticated enough that I don't feel embarassed reading it at University (when technically I should be studying).<br/><br/>This part of the adventure takes place in Egypt, a place I thought would lend to a great deal of stereotype - Tutankhamen, the Pyramids, the Sphinx - you know the deal. Hence I was pleasantly surprised to find</span>
  <span id="freeText12015539840384823541" style="display:none">Another excellent book in this ever developing series. I love that reading this book as a young adult, I still get a lot of value and enjoyment out of it. The cover even looks sophisticated enough that I don't feel embarassed reading it at University (when technically I should be studying).<br /><br />This part of the adventure takes place in Egypt, a place I thought would lend to a great deal of stereotype - Tutankhamen, the Pyramids, the Sphinx - you know the deal. Hence I was pleasantly surprised to find that the facts we learn are less obvious and significantly more interesting. The dam in the Nile for example, and the way that the ruins on one island had to be moved to another when the water level rose.<br /><br />I particularly enjoyed the way that the characters became more fleshed out and showed real human flaws and weaknesses. Both Amy and Dan go through a crisis of faith and come out stronger for it. Even the bad guys start showing a few interesting cracks.<br /><br />All up, 39 Clues is turning into a complex story that is so simple to read that you just absorb the complexity in your stride. I am kept guessing right to the end and even when something obvious has happened, I find myself wondering why I didn't see it coming. A great story with wonderful consistency from book to book despite there being four different authors so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12015539840384823541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14746794198127218546" style="display:none">Book #4. But what clue are we on? Will there be 39 books? Have we only had four clues? It seems like we are probably on clue #11. <br /><br />Okay, so I went on wikipedia and there will be ten books in the series. <br /><br />These are pretty fun kid's books. Better than the Series of Unfortunate Events, not as good as Percy Jackson (which, in turn, is not as good as Artemis Fowl). <br /><br />This series is a quick read. I like the clues and the hunt. I get tired of the getting lost from the au pair and the reality that a hunt like this would be very expensive and time-consuming. The best part about this series is that it is written by multiple authors so a new book comes out about every three months. <br /><br />There is a website for the series and each book comes with clue cards (which I have not seen since I have always read library copies). I went to the website a few months ago on a lunch hour and spent a half hour clicking around and reading back up info. Probably a lot of fun for an 8-14 kid but I wasn't completely sucked in. Also, there are clues hidden in the page numbers of each book. I have not worked them out though. So basically, there is a lot going on that I am not taking advantage of. Perhaps when B is a bit older . . .</span>

  <span id="freeText9813284942039670441" style="display:none">It was very suspenseful and full of mystery. Interested in reading the other books. I loved it! I'm a big fan of suspense and mystery, and this book does it right! The series is interesting and a good book about finding clues and betrayal.<br /><br />The 4th installment in the series, betrayed by their cousins, left alone by their uncle, and no idea where they are, Amy and Dan Cahill are completely lost in Egypt with no one to help them guide through the endless crowd of tourists. With also the fact that they're being tracked down by a Russian ex-KGB agent called Irina Spasky. However, they were able to lose her and crossed paths with a man named Theo who helped them find their grandmother, Nellie. They successfully all regrouped and continued the search for the 39 clues. Will they ever find Grace's secret? Will Amy and Dan find the clue after perilous adventures? Or will they be completely lost forever and fail the challenge? And can they trust ANYONE after everything that's happened to them?<br /><br />That's what makes this book feel like a ticking time bomb. I love the suspense and love the series! This book will want you to keep reading and never put it down! I recommend this book for all ages, young or old.</span>

Along the way they meet old friends of Grace (some helpful, some treacherous) and Uncle Allistaire decides to "come back from the (suppossed) dead" to team up with Amy and Dan once again. Just like the previous books, a lot happens in a short amount of time and the next clue is given up.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473398505?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duffy Pratt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duffy Pratt" href="/user/show/2729963-duffy-pratt">Duffy Pratt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2729963-duffy-pratt?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2729963-duffy-pratt?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473398505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9186271293668252953">Another mediocre installment. Dan and Amy don't seem to be developing at all, while the side characters like Irina and Johah Wizard become more shallow every time they appear. The big mystery here is not the clues, but whether there will ever be any kind of explanation of the Cahill clan. I've given up on the hope that any of this will make sense. There is still a wee bit of fun to be had, but at this point its being overwhelmed by the sheer ridiculousness of it all.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Cf0X1yITupdDcdM/3QQSGW9SwCvLwt3rb03s3+fVHXPMqvZ4EhvflKc2DGJUK1qF4lb5LEPsKYKs1XCLhawSGA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
